"Cultural Work in the Americas" In early April, Envoy Matsunaga will be dispatched to North America to tour Canada, Mexico, and Central and South American countries to conduct specific investigations into cultural cooperation and friendship between these New World countries and Japan. "Cultural Work in Europe" Ambassador Matsudaira, who will return to London in March, will convene the second meeting of ambassadors and ministers to Europe in London to conduct various adjustments in political and economic matters. At the same time, he must also implement friendship and cooperation with various countries in culture to make further efforts. Japanese cultural libraries should be established in major cities around the world. There is a strong desire in major cities of various countries to study Japanese culture, so Japanese cultural libraries should be established to facilitate research and enable people to thoroughly explore the essence of Japanese culture. All preparations should be made. The cities currently planned for the opening of libraries are as follows: New York, San Francisco, Rio de Janeiro, London, Paris, Berlin, Bangkok, Sydney, etc. (9th, Domei News)

Tokyo, Ambassador to Britain Tsuneo Matsudaira has returned to his post after his home leave. He will return to his post in London in mid-March with Foreign Minister Hirota's instructions for Anglo-Japanese harmony. As for the Minister Eden, he will gradually conclude an Anglo-Japanese agreement on trade areas and request British recognition of Japan's East Asian policy. Oil Embargo Against Italy is Likely to be Implemented: Observations of London Insiders 49

However, the approach taken may not be too severe. The report of the League of Nations experts will be published soon.

Regarding the issue of an oil embargo against Italy, according to observations from oil industry and banking experts in London, it is inevitable that discussions will soon turn into action. However, it is predicted that the implementation will not be too severe, so as not to cause the Italian army's supplies to run out. According to technicians with well-informed sources known to this reporter, this is the first time that there is such clear evidence. They also said that the League of Nations, at this time, must implement embargo measures to maintain its prestige, which is not only entirely possible but also its bounden duty. As for the implementation of the oil embargo, it is generally believed that the United States will continue to supply Italy with oil. Therefore, Italy should not regard the embargo as a cause for declaring war and immediately take military action. Furthermore, several organizations supporting the League of Nations in London today issued a declaration demanding that the League of Nations implement an oil embargo, be decisive and not be constrained by the resolutions of the US Congress regarding new neutrality laws, and hesitate. Political figures believe that, judging from the current situation, the cabinet will definitely satisfy the wishes of these organizations. However, people generally believe that if an embargo is implemented, Mussolini can tacitly agree to it within certain limits. Geneva, The report on the oil embargo against Italy, compiled based on the opinions of the small subcommittees on the benefits and harms of the oil embargo, will be published by the Committee of Eighteen next week. (9th, Reuters)

Seven Italian Aircraft Bomb Taishe City 50

The Ah Emperor is Safe and Sound

Seven Italian bombers from Taishe flew to Taishe, where the headquarters of the Ah army is located on the Northern Road, and bombarded the city and nearby houses with incendiary bombs and bombs for over an hour. Their purpose was to kill the Ah Emperor. Several bombs fell near the imperial palace, but the Ah Emperor refused to take shelter and remained safe. It is reported that several holes were shot in the Italian planes, but none crashed. The extent of the damage is currently unknown. There have been no reports of any casualties among foreigners. (9th, Reuters)

Rome, According to a government communiqué issued here, General De Bono, commander-in-chief of the Italian forces in Africa, is consolidating the Italian army's already occupied areas. At the same time, the Italian army is pursuing the enemy in the Southern Road towards the River, while there are no reports from the Northern Road front. (8th, Guomin News)

Results of Paris Talks: Austrian Restoration Setback; Large-Scale Arrests of Left and Right Extremists 52

Vienna, Deputy Chancellor Prince Starhemberg visited the capitals of Britain and France to discuss the issue of the restoration of the Habsburgs with the authorities of those countries. He has now returned. According to what this reporter has learned, the restorationists here had high expectations for the Deputy Chancellor's trip. They initially believed that Yugoslavia's opposition to the Austrian restoration was deeply rooted. The Vice-Chancellor's meeting with Prince Paul of Yugoslavia, the regent of that country, might soften the country's attitude. At the same time, Archduke Otto, the heir to the Habsburgs, is living in exile in Steenokkerzeel, Belgium. The Deputy Chancellor was supposed to visit Belgium to have a face-to-face discussion with the Archduke. However, things turned out unexpectedly, greatly disappointing them. Not only did Prince Paul of Yugoslavia, the regent, avoid meeting with the Deputy Chancellor in Paris, but Archduke Otto also did not meet with the Deputy Chancellor when he visited Paris, believing that a meeting between the two would be inappropriate at this time. In addition, Chancellor Schuschnigg also holds different views on the immediate restoration of the Empire. On the one hand, Archduke Otto is still young, and if he suddenly ascended to the throne, his every word and action would be controlled by the former Queen Zita. On the other hand, Austria's economic difficulties have not yet been overcome, and hasty changes would lead to anger. Yesterday, a restorationist told this reporter that "Archduke Otto should exercise patience at this time," indicating that the Austrian restoration movement has suffered a setback.

Vienna, Today it was learned that after Deputy Chancellor Prince Starhemberg held a series of political meetings in Paris and returned to Austria, the Austrian police immediately launched a nationwide search for communists and National Socialists. France Borrows from Britain; Finance Minister Attends Parliament to Explain 62

Paris: During a meeting of the Finance Committee of the Chamber of Deputies today, Finance Minister Régnier attended and spoke, confirming the rumors of the government negotiating a loan with London. He said that the government was doing this because borrowing in the London market would have lower interest rates than in France. However, these talks are still in the technical research stage and no decision has been made. Régnier also did not agree with the idea that this loan's success depends on granting economic concessions to Britain. (Reuters, 8th)

Paris: Finance Minister Régnier recently attended the Finance Committee of the Chamber of Deputies and explained the issue of France borrowing from Britain. It is said that the treasury needs a total of 7,000,000,000 francs in expenses until June of this year. Although treasury bills can continue to be issued to provide funding, it will be difficult to reach this amount, so it is necessary to resort to borrowing. Negotiations are currently underway in London, and their nature is purely technical. He cannot provide a report at this time, but in any case, Parliament will be notified before the loan is finalized. Régnier also said that investors in the domestic financial market are currently taking a wait-and-see attitude, so the government's recent bond issuance has not been enthusiastically subscribed. The government, aware of this, fears that the continued issuance of treasury bills will not be successful. In addition, the Bank of England can lend to the Bank of France at low interest rates, so negotiations are being held with London to borrow. As for the rumors that Britain is using economic interests as an exchange condition, it is completely untrue. (Havas, 8th)

North Atlantic Aviation Route: Plan About to be Realized; Northern Ireland MP to Question British Government 64

London: The plan to open a North Atlantic aviation route is about to be realized. A Northern Ireland MP in the House of Commons will question the government on this matter. As early as 1931, the "Transatlantic Airways" of Northern Ireland attempted to open a commercial aviation route across the North Atlantic to connect air traffic between North America and Northern Ireland. Most countries have spared no effort in researching and designing for their own interests. Countries such as the UK, US, Germany, and the Netherlands were involved in the above plan. In 1933, Germany and the Netherlands withdrew first, leaving only the UK and the US closely monitoring the matter. The Northern Ireland airline originally believed that it would be able to obtain the support of the British Air Ministry to realize its plan. However, the Air Ministry later favored a certain British company, intending to have it undertake the matter and refusing to provide the necessary facilities to the Northern Ireland company. Therefore, the company recently issued a booklet attacking the government, saying that the so-called British company neither possesses seaplanes capable of flying across the Atlantic on schedule nor has the facilities for landing sites. On the contrary, the Irish company has been preparing for the route for a long time, and its formal opening is expected to be realized. Why does the Air Ministry refuse to provide assistance? It is said that the Northern Ireland MP has threatened to raise this issue to the government. (Havas, 8th)

Rural Economic Miscellany 94

— Edited by Yu Qingtang, Written by Qi Zhi

Long-Absent Hometown Yixing

An Analysis of Rural Poverty

I.

I am grateful for this illness of mine—it gave me the opportunity to return to my hometown (and it is my hometown) for a short stay. For the sake of studying (I still don't understand what use those books I read in middle school and university have for me, except for getting a qualification. So it was just 'studying for the sake of studying'.), for the sake of eating, I had to drift around in various cities. Because I was used to seeing neat roads, tall buildings, beautiful shop windows, noble gentlemen, and imposing foreign dignitaries, when I went back to everything in my hometown where I grew up, it seemed very different from the scenes in my childhood memories, which aroused my novel attention.

II.

It's not entirely because my "horizons are high." Everything in my hometown, in these six or seven years, has changed in many ways. First, in the past, going back always meant taking a train to Wuxi, then a small steamship to Yixing, and then changing to a private boat, which took two days in total. Now it only takes half a day. Whether going back from Nanjing, Shanghai, or Hangzhou, you can take a long-distance bus home from the Jinghang Highway, the Xiyi Highway, and the Yichang (Changzhou) Highway. This is unspeakably convenient for students returning for vacation, merchants rushing on the road, and employees returning to their homes during the holidays. But after all, it has not been able to replace steamships and private boats. Taking a long-distance bus costs almost one cent of silver per mile. One cent of silver is equal to three copper coins, and three copper coins are equal to one large pancake. The cost of taking the bus for more than ten miles can maintain a day's life in the countryside. Thirty or forty miles (or a little more) can be reached by the villagers just by moving their feet. If it is further away, a few hundred cash can be used to take a boat, and on it you can drink tea, chat, and take a nap. Many agricultural products such as rice, sweet potatoes, vegetables, mountain goods, pottery, etc., as well as oil, salt, cloth, etc. from the cities, still rely on shipping. The South has plenty of rivers, and "the five lakes and four seas" are all "free for boats to travel" without spending money. And shipping costs are much lower. Therefore, steamships and scheduled boats still exist, but the equipment is more suitable for the needs of the villagers. As for the price the villagers pay for leaving the fields and leaving the man-made highways, it is just adding some "eye candy": cars like ground tigers, roaring and screaming, foreign women leading foreign dogs, coming and going with her husband, on fine days in spring and autumn, groups of small cars (villagers call private cars small cars to distinguish them from long-distance buses) are full of dignified and gorgeous gentlemen and graceful ladies or young ladies; from time to time, there are entire teams of troops, fully armed, walking or always speeding by on trucks.

Having become accustomed to the tall and majestic ancient city walls of Nanjing, the city walls of Yixing seem like a "fortress" found in northern villages. Inside this city circle, the once seemingly prosperous street when I first entered the city from the countryside—the wide and flat stone-paved road, the neat and uniform gold-lettered signboards, the red lacquer counters, the dazzling array of goods in the display cases—now seems very deserted. The golden and red brilliant colors have faded, because of the long-term erosion of wind and rain without being able to be painted: a few figures in the store are trading in the dim darkness. The bustling villagers who were crowded and shoulder-to-shoulder in the main street are also gone. Everything appears scattered, dim, quiet, and even a little desolate. Walking through a few streets, only a few exceptions were found: several foreign goods stores (like small department stores in Shanghai) are quite developed, completely decorated with the latest style of storefront windows: French Simon cream, Coty perfume, British cold wool fabrics, etc. are displayed with the most attractive patterns, colors and light. In addition, three or four branches of banks have also appeared. This is a newly arrived but very powerful "store," so its buildings are also distinctly black and white, towering majestically. Banks such as Shanghai Bank and Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank mainly operate on agricultural product mortgages, and they have also set up many warehouses in places with convenient transportation in the surrounding countryside, which are used to hold the collateral of the villagers. There are also some occupations that did not exist before, such as newspapers and lawyers, each with several. At first, I thought this was an improvement in the cultural level and legal knowledge of my hometown, but by the time I came out, I had to completely deny it.

III.

As soon as I returned to the P village where my old residence was, the same old things, especially that way of life, immediately evoked my childhood experiences, making me feel very familiar: doing all kinds of farming, transplanting seedlings, harvesting, planting wheat, and chopping firewood according to the progress of the seasons, without any change; even that piece of rice paddy, mulberry garden, vegetable garden, and even a pile of ashes are the same as before. The population has increased a lot, especially the children. A group of ten or twenty children from three or four years old to ten years old are playing in the sunny corner of the threshing ground. The number of households has also increased. Some who have been running docks and working in factories have also returned to the countryside because of the closure of industry and commerce.

The color of poverty has spread throughout this large village, which has three or four hundred households and was once known for its abundance. Although the nearby area is a place of lime production, the walls are eroded with patches of yellow and black. They have not been plastered for many years, thatched grass is used to repair the holes in the tiled roofs, and vegetable gardens are no longer fenced with bamboo strips or bamboo branches, but with sunflower stalks, mulberry branches, and everything that does not require spending money to buy. Everyone has disheveled hair or long hair, because this can save money on haircuts. There is no such thing as single or lined clothes, they wear whatever they can grab. So-called neatness and cleanliness are never thought of by them. After the great drought the year before last, in the spring and summer seasons of last year (1935), only a dozen families in the whole village ate rice. The rest ate coarse grains or went hungry. This had never happened before. The village elementary school is free of charge, but the number of students is decreasing day by day, because spending one or two yuan on books is an extreme luxury (even a bit of a waste) for them, not to mention that children over ten years old can also help their fathers in the fields to cut grass and deliver meals.

Originally, there were many trees and bamboo forests beside the village houses, but now they are all gone. Nanshan, not far from the village, I remember going to the dense forest in the mountains in spring to find orchids when I was a child. When there was wind, I could hear the pine waves filling the valley, scaring my young partners who thought it was a tiger's roar and screaming. Now they have all become bare, denuded mountains! The trees on the mountains have all been cut down. Needless to say, the villagers are so poor that they can't wait to turn everything that can be turned into cash into money.

The villagers have completely lost their credit due to delays. The village shops will absolutely no longer extend credit, and accommodating loans requires extreme favour or more than 20% interest. Indeed, money is the most lacking thing in the countryside. Poor, poor, that is its whole appearance. I never thought that my hometown—with mountains behind it and water in front of it, "fields crisscrossing," "houses neatly arranged," and "happily self-sufficient" P village—has become so dilapidated in these few years.

Page 8

Japan-Philippines Association and China-Philippines Association　Philippine Correspondence 95

The Japanese side is proceeding very rapidly, while we are extremely neglected

The most essential claim of the United States' approval of the Philippine Islands Independence Act is to protect the interests of American farmers. Therefore, the Tydings-McDuffie Independence Act stipulates that "Philippine sugar can be transported to the United States duty-free, not exceeding 850,000 tons per year, coconut oil 200,000 tons, abaca 3 million pounds... After independence is realized, American goods can be shipped to the Philippines, and the United States can collect all import taxes." Sugar, coconut, and abaca are important local products of the Philippine Islands and also the basic source of wealth for the Philippine economy. Judging from the 1933 statistics, these three local products accounted for 88% of the total exports, that is, out of 211,542,105 Philippine pesos, they accounted for 187,550,125 pesos. After the Philippine Islands becomes independent, the United States will adopt a tariff protection policy, and these various local products will be subject to tariff restrictions. How can they be sold to the United States as much as possible? They will inevitably have to find new markets. The targets for finding new markets are China and Japan, because China has a large population and huge consumption, and Japan has a booming industry and a lack of raw materials, both of which can absorb local products from the Philippines. Currently, Filipinos are planning how to transport agricultural products to China and Japan. In the future, in order to realize this plan, it is necessary to vigorously promote China-Philippines friendship and Japan-Philippines friendship, or even conclude a most-favored-nation trade treaty with the two countries, so that China and Japan can absorb their local products as much as possible. If our country's authorities can take this opportunity to contact the Philippine Islands, the status of overseas Chinese in the Philippines can also be slightly consolidated. The Japanese are paying very close attention to this. The Japanese side has always been actively committed to developing Nanyang trade. Now that it encounters this opportunity, how can it easily let it go? Therefore, in the past year, personnel dispatched by the Japanese government and the private sector have come to the Philippines one after another. Their purpose is to connect feelings and communicate culture, and they have established the Japan-Philippines Association in Tokyo, with Duke Tokugawa as the president. When the Philippine autonomous government was established, Japan originally planned to send Duke Tokugawa as a special envoy to the Philippines to celebrate, but it was later stopped because the United States did not want to overdo it. The intentions of both parties can be guessed. Not long ago, the former Japanese ambassador to the Philippines, Horibuchi, went to Australia to return the visit. When he passed through Manila, he mentioned this matter to President Quezon. Quezon said, "After the establishment of the Japan-Philippines Association, preparations will also be made here." Therefore, recently, Japanese residents in the Philippines, together with some Philippine celebrities, jointly organized the Philippine branch of the Tokyo Japan-Philippines Association in Manila. The preparatory office is located at the Japanese consulate, and personnel from the Japanese consulate are in charge of organizing matters. It is expected that after the branch is established, it will communicate information about Japanese-Philippine cultural institutions from time to time, and promote each other's organized tourist groups to visit and investigate education and investigate economic conditions. It is also heard that a few years ago, Japanese residents in the Philippines established the Greater Asia Association Philippine Branch, and in addition to Filipinos and Japanese, there were also Indians joining. In January of this year, the Greater Asia Association hosted a Japan-Philippines friendship New Year banquet in Manila. The Japanese military attache stationed in Taipei, Takeo Ota, who came to the Philippines to inspect Japanese residents in Davao, Mindanao, specially attended the banquet and gave a speech on Japan-Philippines friendship. Their method of contacting Filipinos can be said to be consistent from the government to the private sector, proceeding vigorously, and their ambition is certainly not small.

Looking back at our country, although the political, business, and academic circles organized a Philippine tour group to the Philippines last year, staying for more than a week, the Chinese and Philippine sides had banquets and receptions every night. When they were about to return home, they proposed to political and business celebrities to organize a China-Philippines Association, the purpose of which was to connect China and Philippine feelings and promote commerce between the two sides. Overseas Chinese in the Philippines hoped that it would be quickly realized, and held two or three meetings to decide on the articles of association and sent them to Shanghai, but so far there has been no news of any progress. The so-called China-Philippines Association proposal is probably indefinitely shelved.

Ice Floes Outside Dagukou　Frozen for Over Two Hundred Li 96

Shipping in Bohai Bay Completely Suspended　Countless Ships Trapped Outside the Port

Tianjin Correspondence: The weather in North China has been unusually cold for nearly half a month. The normal air pressure is constantly below fourteen or fifteen degrees. The water route from Tianjin to outside Dagukou was already heavily frozen from the beginning of last month. The river channel is sealed by ice and snow. Although it slightly bursts during high tide, it still freezes as before after cracking. The Haihe River between Tianjin and Tanggu is about two feet thick with ice. Ling ice accumulates on the black gully side of the sand barrier outside Tanggu to Dagukou, freezing to six or seven feet to one zhang. Small passenger and cargo boats and powerful tugboats of various companies are blocked and cannot travel. From Dagukou to the north along the coast of Bohai Bay for two or three hundred miles, all is frozen solid. The ports of Qinhuangdao are also frozen like a pond. Looking as far as the eye can see, there is no end in sight. It feels as if the world of the Arctic water has been moved before your eyes. Chinese and foreign passenger and cargo ships all suffer when they travel outside Dagukou. For over a week, no ships have entered or exited the port. Powerful ships such as Swire's Shuntian and New Shengjing, Osaka Company's Changan Maru and Changjiang Maru, Dalian Company's Changping Maru and Tianjin Maru, Zhengji Company's Tali and Fuli, and Tongshun Company's Xintai, totaling dozens, are all frozen and stranded inside and outside the port. As of the 7th, a total of seventeen large ships were trapped outside Dagukou, and thirteen large ships were trapped between Dagukou and Tanggu inside Dagukou. Countless sailboats and small steamers were frozen and unable to sail. Ruikang, an agent of Tianjin Shipping Company, was frozen outside Dagukou and urgently telegraphed the Tianjin Customs Port Director for help, hoping to send coal and grain as soon as possible. Zhengji Company's Tongli ship tried to risk sailing from outside the port, but the rudder was broken and could not be turned. Other ships of various companies trapped outside the port were panicked because food and fuel could not be supplied. Small vendors near Dagukou went to sell eggs and bread on the ice because the ships outside the port could not move. Eggs cost one yuan each, and bread costs six or seven yuan per pound. Each vendor makes a profit of three times. The Tianjin Customs Port Authority and the Haihe Engineering Bureau recently sent five icebreakers to try to break the ice outside the port. As a result, three were destroyed and the remaining two froze as they broke the ice. The route was still impassable. On the 6th, Tianjin Shipping Company's new icebreaking tugboat Tianxing arrived at Tanggu after breaking through the ice outside the port, carrying small workers from Tianjin barges. One rudder and wheel of the ship was damaged. The flow of Ling ice at Dagukou Gate is becoming more rapid. Ships without strong horsepower and a sturdy hull will inevitably be pushed onto the ice mountain by the water when passing through. Dalian Company's Yijin Maru was frozen in the ice mountain on Dagukou North Port and has been there for two weeks. I don't know if it has fallen. According to the captain of the Tianxing tugboat, which went outside the port to rescue the Tianjin barge on the 6th, at 10 am today, the ship departed from Tanggu Wharf. Before arriving at Dagukou Wharf, it encountered the Haihe Engineering Bureau's icebreaker Qingling going out of the port at the same time. This ship was in front. By the time it reached Heigou, the Qingling had fallen behind by two li. This ship was about one li away from the Tianjin barge and could not move forward. The ice there was very thick, six or seven feet, and endless, over two hundred li. Seventeen ships were trapped by the water outside the port that could be seen with the naked eye. This ship ultimately failed to rescue the Tianjin ship, etc. Yesterday (the 6th), various shipping merchants in Tianjin held a meeting at Jardine, Matheson & Co. to discuss ways to rescue the ships trapped outside the port. It lasted a long time, but no decision was made. In the end, they had to let nature take its course. Since the ships did not enter the port, the prices of imported goods in Tianjin have risen sharply in recent days. Fresh fruits, etc., mostly come from Japan. Due to the shortage of goods, prices have risen even more severely. The Tianjin Customs Port Director is deeply concerned that various ships will recklessly enter the port regardless of the danger and has issued Notice No. 1, stating that the ice situation in Bohai Bay and outside the Haihe estuary is extremely bad. Local water vessels cannot help. All ships that pass through the bay in the future shall be responsible for any accidents. In addition to being submitted to the Port Affairs Division, this notice is hereby issued to all Chinese and foreign shipping merchants for compliance. (7th)

Liu Guitang Bandit Troops Fled to Henan and Were Defeated 97

The Bandits' Ammunition is Exhausted and They Are Weak, and They Can Be Eliminated Soon

Kaifeng Correspondence: After Liu Guitang's bandit troops fled to Henan Province, they raped, looted, and disturbed the people. After being intercepted and attacked by the 32nd Army and the 95th Division, as well as the militia teams of various counties, they all fled to the Shunping area of Hebei. Several hundred of Liu's bandits were severely suppressed by the 95th Division in Jiangjiaji in the southeast of Shexian County. On the 4th, they fled to Paihuai Town in the southwest of Wu'an County, and were intercepted by the Huang Guanghua unit of the 32nd Army. Liu's bandits then fled north to the Hundred Officials River Bottom and other places, and were again intercepted by the Wu'an militia team, killing more than ten bandits, capturing eight alive, and seizing three guns. The remaining bandit troops turned to flee east from the northeast of Wu'an to Furun Village, and continued to flee towards the North Shahetou direction. At present, there are very few bandit troops left. Some fled into the mountains, trying their best to avoid contact with the army. The bandits' ammunition is exhausted and they are weak and not worth attacking. Shang Zhen received a telegram from Huang Guanghua on the 5th, stating that Liu's bandits had taken the opportunity to flee back from the east and west Jiaojing to Paihuai Town via Guzhen, and arrived near Tongle. The division's Zhang regiment and others will use machine guns and mules to form a cavalry of 70 men to search and suppress them with all their strength. It is not difficult to eliminate them. In addition to ordering the division to quickly dispatch teams to transport them by rail to Yulian Town, Linluo Guanxi to suppress and block them, so as to prevent them from fleeing east, Chairman Shang also ordered the militia groups in various counties in northern Henan to conduct a thorough investigation of the scattered bandits, so as to avoid them hiding among the people and making a comeback.

Xiamen　Smuggling is Still Rampant 98

Although Customs Destroys Smuggling Ships, It Still Cannot Be Slightly Curbed　Sugar is Almost All Smuggled Goods, and Matches Are Also Affected

Xiamen Correspondence: Southern Fujian and Taiwan are only separated by a narrow strip of water, and sailboats can reach it overnight in narrow places. The wind of tax evasion and smuggling is extremely prevalent along the coast. Although the customs has increased anti-smuggling ships and strictly suppressed smuggling, news of cracking down on smuggling is heard every day. In addition to setting up ships to collect smuggled goods, the crew members are also severely punished, but it still cannot be curbed. The wind of smuggling is due to the fact that the seized smuggled goods and smuggling ships are auctioned in Xiamen, and they are usually bought at a low price by the original owners. Therefore, since last autumn, the Xiamen Customs has transported all seized smuggled goods to Shanghai for auction, and the smuggling sailboats are sacrificed by being dismantled and sold as broken wood, and the engines of motorboats are dismantled and transported to Shanghai for auction, and the hulls are also sacrificed by being dismantled. The customs now has a large shipyard on Gulangyu Island, specializing in dismantling these ships, selling the wood to people as fuel. The waste wood is piled up like a mountain, and sometimes it is felt that the money from selling the wood is not enough to cover the demolition wages, so they open fire and sink them. However, although the anti-smuggling is strict, the smugglers are the same as before. From this, it can be seen that the coastal fishing industry is declining and the freight of civil ships is sluggish, causing fishermen and shipworkers to have no work to do, and many of them take risks. On the other hand, it shows that there are many private merchants along the coast, and their role is to directly monopolize the market, making it impossible for legitimate merchants who operate honestly to do anything, and indirectly using the customs to gradually eliminate coastal fishing boats, and to catch them all in one fell swoop. Their plan is truly poisonous and harsh. Ordinary shipworkers do not consider the pros and cons, and sacrifice the entire ship at the cost of one or two hundred yuan. The poverty of the society can be imagined. It is found that sugar is the largest smuggled product in southern Fujian, followed by kerosene and matches. In January, the sugar officially taxed and imported by Xiamen Customs was only 30 packages transported from Taiwan by Shunmei. In January, the customs cracked down on smuggled sugar, totaling 1,070 packages. 1,171 packages were transported to Shanghai for auction. The number of smuggled sugar that can be surveyed at Xiamen alone is 684 packages. As for the inland, the private sugar that is transported from Jiuzhen Founan Bridge in Zhangpu to the counties under Zhangzhou, from Wuyu in Haicang to Shima, from Shenqu in Yongning to Quanzhou, and from Daxiaodeng in Lianhe to Tong'an cannot be counted. As for matches, in Fujian Province, in addition to Japanese matches, the domestic Great China Company also sells a lot. In the past two years, the sales in Zhangzhou and Quanzhou inland reached more than 7,000 boxes per month. For tax-paid imports, each box must be sold for 42 yuan, while Japanese matches, which are smuggled in, only sell for 26 yuan per box, which is a profit of three or four yuan. As a result, domestic products have been severely hit. In the 24th year, the Great China Company's business lost 400,000 yuan. Therefore, if the government does not crack down on smuggling, not only will merchants not be able to support it, but the country's tax revenue will also be affected. Recently, the Ministry of Finance has paid close attention to cracking down on the smuggling of matches. In addition to approving the establishment of branches in Jiuzhen and Fotanju, Zhangpu, where the Fujian Unified Tax Office is located, it also telegraphed the Xiamen Customs to pay attention to anti-smuggling. In the past, the auction prices of the customs' cracked and auctioned goods were often cheaper than those of tax-paid imports, and domestic goods were still hit. Now the auction prices of foreign matches are reviewed and determined by the Unified Tax Office, and they are not sold at reduced prices. This year, domestic matches have begun to improve. Great China has increased from 3,000 boxes sold per month last winter to 4,000 boxes. (February 8th)

Fujian　Survey of the Banking Industry 99

There are a total of twenty-two banks

Fuzhou Correspondence: According to a survey by the Statistics Office of the Provincial Government, there are currently twenty-two banks in Fujian Province, which can be divided into three types:　Foreign merchants' banks, there are three in total: Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation, located in Fuzhou and Xiamen; Bank of Taiwan, located in Fuzhou and Xiamen; and Banque de l'Indochine, located in Xiamen. In the past, both Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation and Bank of Taiwan issued notes, but they have now been withdrawn.　Chinese-run banks with headquarters in Shanghai and branches in this province, there are twelve in total: Central Bank of China, located in eight places: Fuzhou, Xiamen, Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, Yanping, Pucheng, Jian'ou, and Sandu; Bank of China, located in three places: Fuzhou, Xiamen, and Quanzhou; Bank of Communications, located in two places: Fuzhou and Xiamen; Farmers Bank of China, located in four places: Fuzhou, Xiamen, Pucheng, and Yanping; China Industrial Bank, located in two places: Fuzhou and Xiamen; China Merchants Bank, located in Xiamen; Chung Nan Bank, located in Xiamen; Sin Tai Bank, located in three places: Fuzhou, Yanping, and Pucheng. The above eight banks all issue notes. The National Commercial Bank, located in Xiamen; Overseas Chinese Bank, located in Xiamen; Chung Hing Bank, located in Xiamen; Xinhua Bank, located in Xiamen. The above four banks do not issue notes.　Banks run by Fujianese, there are seven in total: Provincial Bank of Fujian, located in Fuzhou and Xiamen; Hua Nan Bank, Commercial Bank, Hui Nan Bank, Yu Nong Bank, Fu Feng Bank, all located in Fuzhou; Putian Industrial Bank, located in Putian. The above banks, except for the Provincial Bank of Fujian, do not issue notes. In terms of commercial status, the Bank of China and Chung Nan Bank are the most important. In terms of agricultural status, the Farmers Bank of China is the most important. In terms of political status, the Central Bank and the Provincial Bank are the most important. The Central Bank originally concurrently handled the two functions of the national treasury and the provincial treasury. Since the Provincial Bank of Fujian opened in October last year, the provincial treasury has been transferred to the bank to act as an agent. Now the Central Bank is changing its organization to become a reserve bank for national banks, specializing in adjusting finance and stabilizing currency, and does not engage in ordinary commercial bank business. There is no need to set up offices everywhere, so it has been decided to abolish the Yanping, Jian'ou, Pucheng, and four offices under the jurisdiction of the Fuzhou branch, and the Zhangzhou and Quanzhou offices under the jurisdiction of the Xiamen branch. The Provincial Bank of Fujian, on the other hand, is developing its business day by day, and plans to set up offices in Zhangzhou, Quanzhou, Tingzhou, Xianyou, Changle, Fuqing, Fuan, Tong'an, Zhangpu, Chong'an, Putian, Yanping, and Longyan in the near future. The heads of each office have been appointed and ordered to go to prepare immediately. It is found that the bank's capital was originally set at one million yuan, and the provincial government first allocated 500,000 yuan and issued one million yuan of fractional notes. It is now planned to raise another 500,000 yuan and issue another one million yuan of fractional notes to meet the needs. (February 8th)

Lu Province's 108 Counties Divided into Administrative Regions 100

Abolishing the Experimental Zone Name, Restoring the Commissioner System, Initially Establishing Three Zones: Ji'ning, Heze, and Linyi

Jinan Correspondence: In order to increase administrative efficiency, the provincial government established an administrative region last year in Ji'ning, encompassing fourteen counties. Wang Shaochang was appointed as the administrative inspector commissioner. Later, the name was changed to the County Administration Construction Experimental Zone. Over the past year, significant progress has been made in public training and organization. Therefore, the Provincial Chairman, Han Fuqu, has decided to expand the initiative to the entire province of 108 counties, dividing them into twelve zones. Recently, Heze and Linyi have been added, totaling three zones including the one established last year. Regarding the name, it is proposed to abolish the name "Experimental Zone" and restore the title of Administrative Inspector Commissioner. In addition to Wang Shaochang continuing to serve in Ji'ning, Liang Zhonghua is internally designated for the Heze zone, and Zhang Liyuan for the Linyi zone. Currently, Liang Zhonghua, Liang Shuming, Zhang Liyuan, Sun Zherang, and Wang Shaochang have all been summoned to Jinan to discuss everything. Today (the 6th), Han hosted a banquet at the provincial government for Liang Zhonghua and others, inviting the secretary-general, department heads, and commissioners to attend. During the banquet, there was considerable discussion about the functions and powers of each zone. Han offered many opinions. After the banquet, key figures gathered in the secretary-general's office for detailed talks. A general outline for the organization has already been fully agreed upon. The Administrative Inspector Commissioner will be a senior position, appointed by the provincial government's political affairs meeting and submitted to the Ministry of Interior for forwarding to the Executive Yuan for record. The method remains the promotion of rural agricultural studies and the integration of politics and education, with no major changes from the previous County Administration Construction Experimental Zone. However, there are minor conflicts in functions and powers with various departments, and it is scheduled for Saturday (the 8th) at 8:00 AM for Liang Zhonghua and others to discuss further details with department representatives. If a solution is reached, a final decision can be made, and it may be submitted to the provincial government's political affairs meeting for implementation next week, possibly established around March. As for the regional issues, they are still under study. Chairman Han previously divided the County Administration Construction Experimental Zone into fourteen counties, which was considered too large, and it is proposed to reduce the scope. The Ji'ning zone will be set at ten counties, the Heze zone at nine counties, and the Linyi zone at eight counties, totaling twenty-seven counties. In addition to the original Ji'ning, Wenshang, Dongping, Yuncheng, Yucheng, Heze, Jiaxiang, Juye, Dingtao, Yutai, Jinxiang, Shanxian, Chengwu, and Caoxian, thirteen new counties will be added. The names of the counties have not yet been announced, but the authorities have previously indicated that Linyi, Tancheng, Yishui, Feixian, Mengyin, Rizhao, Juxian, Zou, Teng, and Yi counties, etc., would be included. Calculating, there are already twenty-four counties, leaving only three more needed. The larger Qufu, Ningyang, Ziyang, and Sishui counties may be included.

Saving from Disaster is Saving Lives. Donate One More Coin, Save One More Life.

Songjiang: Tense Situation of Screening and Investigating Opium Smokers 101

The government is strictly banning opium smoking with a four-year plan for complete eradication, showing strong determination. At the beginning of the general registration of opium smokers, many were hesitant and evasive, resulting in many omissions. According to the law, those who smoke privately without a license will be punished. Considering carefulness and leniency, the government has specially organized self-renewal registration as a way for unlicensed opium smokers to self-reflect and awaken. The provincial department specially appointed Inspector Ren Yingcang to Songjiang to supervise. Under County Magistrate Li's leadership, starting from the first of this month, they have been dispatching daily to each district to urge the district, township, and baojia heads to screen and investigate. Simultaneously, armed police are being led to screen and investigate door-to-door. As of yesterday, over four thousand people have been registered, with over three thousand having obtained licenses. However, district and township chiefs are still screening and investigating, with possibly over a thousand still remaining. Now that the self-renewal registration deadline is approaching, the county magistrate has specially called a meeting of the township chiefs of the first district at 1:00 PM on the ninth to urge them to expedite and ensure no omissions. It is reported that County Magistrate Li will still need to go to each district to supervise starting from the thirteenth.

Kunshan: Usage of Relief Association Funds 102

The wartime relief association organized in this county during the Shanghai war has been established for four years. Now that the association's relief efforts have come to an end, it will soon be dissolved. The remaining funds total over 18,300 yuan. The subsequent allocation of funds has been decided as follows: 2,500 yuan for industrial recovery expenses, 4,000 yuan donated for the construction of the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall, 2,000 yuan to increase grain reserves, and 9,000 yuan for expanding relief services. The remaining over 800 yuan will be allocated after the dissolution.

Suzhou: Hunger Strike Turmoil at Wujiang Prison 103

Five robbers, including Lu Aweng, detained in Wujiang County Prison, were banned from gambling by Warden Cheng Gou. Dissatisfied, they instigated over 140 inmates to go on a hunger strike starting at 3:00 PM on the eighth to intimidate. Warden Cheng, upon hearing the news, immediately tried to persuade them himself, but to no avail. He immediately reported to County Magistrate Xu for instructions. County Magistrate Xu immediately dispatched a security brigade for defense to prevent any accidents. At the same time, he personally went to persuade them, explaining the advantages and disadvantages, and brought out Lu Aweng and others, shackling them and transferring them to another prison. By about 6:00 PM, the turmoil subsided. On the ninth, the details of the incident were reported to Chief Judge Zhu of the Jiangsu High Court.

Jiangyin: Actively Repairing Riverfront Sluice Gates 104

The Jiangnan Water Conservancy Engineering Office, in order to regulate water conservancy in various counties in Jiangnan, plans to repair various riverfront sluice gates. Personnel have been dispatched for surveying. In Jiangyin, Huangtian Port, Huangshan Port, and Xia Port are the most expensive. Currently, Huangshan Port, Xia Port, and Shen Port sluice gates will be repaired first, with each costing about three to four thousand yuan.

Changshu: Celebration Meeting of Traditional Chinese Medicine and Music Circles 105

The Legislative Yuan passed the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations in the winter of the 22nd year of the Republic [1933], but they were not implemented. It was not until January 22nd of this year that the National Government officially promulgated them. Currently, local traditional Chinese medicine and music circles are holding a three-day celebration meeting from the ninth to the eleventh of this month. Various pharmacies are decorated with lanterns and selling medicines at reduced prices. As for the traditional Chinese medicine community, over fifty members gathered yesterday to hold a celebration commemorative meeting and passed the following resolutions: 1. Designate January 22nd as a permanent commemorative day for traditional Chinese medicine. 2. No consultation fees will be charged on this day. 3. A celebration meeting will be held every year on this day. 4. Send telegrams to President Chiang and Jiao Yitang of the Central National Medical Hall to express gratitude.

Yangzhou: Salt Transport Deputy's Instruction to Maintain Embankment Works 106

Over a hundred workers, including boat laborers and salt shore employees from Twelve Embankments and Eighteen Gangs, came to Yangzhou to petition various party and government agencies and the Huainan Salt Transport Deputy, expressing their wish to address the critical situation. The representatives, including Yang Yusheng, petitioned the Salt Transport Deputy's Office, stating the urgency of the situation and requesting the immediate allocation of transport to alleviate the suffering. The following instruction was received: "The petition is noted. According to the representatives' presentation to this office, temporarily considering the extenuating circumstances, the four-shore office of this office will convene relevant shore transporters as soon as possible within a feasible range to provide maintenance and relief. The representatives must maintain order and not make excessive demands, which may disrupt local security and violate the law. It should be known that the allocation of transport is the responsibility of the Lianghuai Salt Transport Envoy, who has a unified adjustment plan. Transporters cannot make arrangements at will, nor can they solely consider the needs of the boat laborers. If there are necessary petition matters, they can only be submitted in writing to the transport envoy for review and compliance. Repeatedly gathering crowds to negotiate with transporters is akin to causing disturbances and is undesirable. In addition to informing the office, you should be informed accordingly."

Nantong: Adulterous Woman from Yu Dong Strangles Old Aunt 107

Gu Wangshi, a woman from Qinren Township, Yu Dong, was having an affair with her paternal cousin, Gu Haitao, while her husband was away doing business. Hindered by the surveillance of her husband’s aunt, Gu Zhaoshi, she strangled her to death at night and buried the body in the fields. The district office discovered the crime and reported it to the Nantong District Court. A prosecutor went to examine the body, exhumed it, and found the hemp rope still around her neck. Gu Tushi and Gu Haitao were arrested. After interrogation by the prosecutor, they were taken into custody.

Chen Zhenwen, a police officer from the Jiaxing County Police Brigade, fled on the ninth, taking a wooden-holster gun and over ten bullets. The county ordered a search and arrest and detained his guarantor, Chen Guisheng, ordering him to provide bail and search for him. Yesterday, it was reported that the fourth squad of the county defense team outside the north gate of Taiping Tree said that the fugitive police officer Chen Zhenwen was hiding in the home of Chen Shun and Chen Ren at No. 15 Shangnan Street. The squad leader, Lin Songnian, led armed team members to search and found Chen Zhenwen on top of the bed. They found a 701769 wooden-holster gun and eight bullets (six already loaded) on his chest. After taking him into custody, he was transferred to headquarters and sent to the county government. After interrogation by the county government, the fugitive police officer was sent to the district headquarters detention center to await review.

Educational Broadcast Special

The Occurrence and Prevention of Diseases (Part 2) 110

— Jin Baoshan, Technical Official of the Ministry of Health

Dear listeners, today I will continue to talk about the "Occurrence and Prevention of Diseases" that I didn't finish last time. Regarding this topic, remember that last time we finished talking about the occurrence of diseases. Now we will talk about how to prevent diseases before they occur, as well as prevention methods.

I have already said above that now, because of the evolution of society, there are more and more opportunities for human health to be robbed. Therefore, in order to maintain our lives and protect our health, we should try our best to adapt to this new environment. Medical facilities are one way to help mankind adapt to the new environment. Medicine has gradually progressed from an extremely naive and obscure level to today's scientific medicine, and the effectiveness of disease elimination has also gradually increased. In the past, patients with syphilis could only let it rot naturally for ten or eight years. Now there are special medicines that can be injected. As long as it is treated early, the root of the disease can be removed. In the past, there were many diseases that could not be cured. Once you got sick, you had to prepare a coffin and wait to die. Now there are medicines that can be cured. This is the benefit that modern scientific medicine gives to society and mankind. However, we are still not satisfied with this method of disease removal, because seeking medical treatment when sick is the second and last resort. Let's not talk about the trouble of medicine and the suffering of surgery, and the economic losses during the illness period. Even if there are diseases that can be cured, there are still considerable risks, because many diseases, although treated by doctors, still depend on their natural good course. If the course is poor, even if the doctor exhausts his wisdom, it is difficult to save him. Therefore, it is better to repair the house before it rains than to dig a well when you are thirsty. Paying attention to prevention in advance. In fact, most diseases can be prevented. The Western proverb "An ounce of prevention is worth a pound of cure" has become the golden rule of the medical community. This proactive disease elimination method is the most important part of modern acoustics: "Preventive Medicine". The purpose of preventive medicine is to eliminate various internal causes of disease, thereby improving the health of the people, preventing external causes from acting on the body or invading the body and causing effects, so as to prevent the occurrence of diseases. Its ultimate goal is to enable all mankind to enjoy the richest life and give society the greatest contribution - to obtain real health.

The fundamental way to prevent disease is for everyone to have a healthy life and a hygienic environment: strive to promote personal health, and at the same time accept the special disease prevention methods given to us by science - that is, "vaccination". However, we must know that people are not isolated in society. One person gets sick, and it can affect the second person. If the environment in society is unhygienic, the personal environment will naturally suffer. Therefore, we must go further. This is to work hard to assist in the construction of public health services. Now I will briefly describe these aspects below.

Personal healthy life Personal healthy life includes both physical and psychological aspects. To obtain this kind of healthy life, the first step is to have the knowledge to maintain physical health - that is, common medical and health knowledge. The second step is to use this knowledge to develop correct ideals and attitudes, and earnestly transform our whole life into hygiene. The most important points in personal healthy life are as follows: First, pay attention to nutrition, because the structure of the human body and the work of various functions all originate from food. Therefore, when choosing food, you should distribute it properly so that it can supply various needs of the body. The same is true for the quality of food as for the quantity. Second, pay attention to rest. Our daily work causes fatigue in various parts of the body, so there must be appropriate rest to maintain the health of the body. Sleep is the best way to rest. People with insomnia, because the body only consumes and does not compensate, gradually become thin, health deteriorates, and diseases are prone to occur. On average, each person should sleep at least eight hours a day. Third, pay attention to cleanliness, because uncleanliness is the biggest obstacle to health; unclean food not only hinders digestion, but also has the possibility of causing gastrointestinal diseases; unclean teeth are prone to tooth decay and can also cause other serious diseases such as nephritis; unclean skin directly induces various skin diseases and indirectly affects the body's metabolism - that is, physiological functions. Fourth, pay attention to normal excretion. Waste products produced by the human body due to various physiological functions, as well as the remaining residue after food is digested, must be excreted from the body in order to maintain the health of the body. The excretion of these wastes takes place through the lungs, skin, large intestine, and kidneys. In order to promote the excretion of the lungs, the indoor air should be constantly circulated, and you should often go outdoors to enjoy the benefits of fresh air; for the skin, you should bathe often and pay attention to cleanliness; to promote the excretion of the large intestine, you should have a bowel movement at a fixed time every day, so that it can become a habit. Eating more fruits and vegetables is also very beneficial; as for promoting kidney excretion, the most important thing is to drink more boiled water, at least six large glasses a day. The key is to exercise, because appropriate and moderate exercise can promote blood circulation, so that the water and heat of endocrine can be evenly distributed throughout the body, and at the same time, it can increase the body's excretion and promote the body's nutrition. Sixth, pay attention to cultivating a fulfilling spiritual life, which means training individuals to be able to cope with various environmental situations and various problems in life with ease. To achieve this goal, you must cultivate personal self-reliance, self-esteem, and a broad mind that is not selfish. In your spare time, you should also pay attention to engaging in legitimate entertainment. The "diabetes" we talked about the day before yesterday is a disease of abnormal "metabolism". The main reason is that there is not enough "islet purple" produced by the pancreas. People with diabetes, if they are careful in their diet and eat less starchy and sugary foods, and at the same time keep their entire life in a normal state and not contrary to health principles, can at least reduce the disease. As for the external causes of disease, such as the "lung disease" example I gave the day before yesterday, we know that bacteria are difficult to attack people who pay attention to hygiene and have a healthy constitution. Moreover, tuberculosis bacteria come from the sputum of people with tuberculosis or the excretions of the affected area. If we do not spit everywhere, and cover our mouths and noses with a handkerchief when talking, laughing, coughing, or sneezing, separate the patient's utensils, and place the patient's sputum and the excretions of the affected area in a fixed place and disinfect them at any time, this is simply cutting off the entry and exit of tuberculosis bacteria completely. Since the route of infection is cut off, the disease will naturally not be transmitted. If we can take a step further and send all people who have this disease and are contagious to hospitals or sanatoriums for isolation, it will be even safer.

Vaccination Vaccination, commonly known as vaccination, is a special disease prevention method that science has given us and is very reliable. As we said the day before yesterday, the human body has a kind of immunity that can resist infectious diseases. This immunity can be natural or acquired. Modern medicine has been able to use artificial methods to make human tissues develop acquired immunity to resist certain infectious diseases. This artificial method is to inject a small amount of dead bacteria or viruses into the human body, which is enough to stimulate human tissues to produce immunity but not enough to cause disease. It has now been proven that there are valuable vaccinations, such as vaccination against smallpox, injection of diphtheria toxoid to prevent diphtheria, injection of typhoid cholera vaccine to prevent typhoid and cholera, injection of Pasteur vaccine to increase resistance to plague, and so on. We people living in this dangerous environment should try our best to accept this scientific method and not neglect it in the slightest.

Environmental hygiene Paying attention to environmental hygiene is the best way to eliminate the transmission route of bacteria. Many diseases are transmitted due to unsanitary environments. For example, enteric infectious diseases - such as typhoid, cholera, dysentery - are caused by feces containing these bacteria contaminating water sources, or by flies or other carriers of bacteria transmitting the bacteria in the feces to food, leading to infectious spread. Therefore, if we can pay attention to improving the water supply equipment, protecting the cleanliness of the water source, installing screens on the doors and windows of kitchens and dining rooms, installing fly-proof equipment, disinfecting feces before discarding them, or installing sewers, and then introducing all the feces into a public breeding site and disinfecting them, this will not only prevent flies from breeding, but also prevent the water source and food from being contaminated by bacteria, and the disease will not be transmitted. As for the houses where individuals live, the environment around the houses, and all public entertainment venues, etc., if they can strictly comply with hygienic rules, they will be of great benefit to health and disease prevention, especially for respiratory infectious diseases, such as colds, flu, pneumonia, etc., it is more effective. Eliminating stagnant pools of water, ditches, and removing weeds to prevent mosquitoes from breeding can prevent malaria, relapsing fever, elephantiasis, etc., because these diseases are transmitted by mosquitoes. Therefore, environmental hygiene occupies an important position in disease prevention.

In summary, the various facilities and methods to prevent the occurrence of diseases are nothing more than first making the general public understand the causes of diseases, starting with a healthy personal life, and then proceeding to accept various vaccinations and improve environmental hygiene. All of these are very important. However, individual ability is limited, and we need the ability of the entire society to cooperate, so that we can achieve easy success. Therefore, after 1848, all advanced countries and societies seeking human happiness have an organization called public health. So now I will briefly introduce this public health organization as an ending: Public health is a social organization used to prevent disease, prolong life, and promote human health. This organization seeks environmental hygiene, prevents infectious diseases, instills personal hygiene knowledge, and organizes public medical and health institutions in order to achieve early diagnosis and prevention of various diseases, and to enable individuals to have suitable living conditions to maintain health. Simply put, public health is a social organization for preventing disease and seeking happiness for mankind. Its scope is very broad, including medical management, medical relief, suppression and prevention of various infectious diseases, industrial hygiene, school hygiene, maternal and child hygiene, environmental hygiene, hygienic experiments, vital statistics, implementation of health education, research on public health undertakings, training of health workers, etc. The above-mentioned facilities can directly reduce the mortality rate of the population and the disease rate in society, and indirectly increase social productivity and enrich the social economy. I only need to cite a few more obvious examples to prove that public health can indeed seek happiness for society and mankind.

Increased life expectancy - In the sixteenth century, the average life expectancy in European countries was only about 21 years old, but now several countries - such as Australia and New Zealand - have increased the average life expectancy to 60 years old. A large part of this has been added in the last fifty years following the progress of scientific medicine. The average life expectancy in our country, where scientific medicine has not yet developed, is still around 30 years old, which clearly shows the relationship between medical development and life expectancy.

The success of the Panama Canal - This is an example of overcoming disease with human power. When the French started digging the Panama Canal, because malaria was rampant, 1,500 out of every 100,000 workers died from the disease. Because the losses in terms of both human lives and economy were too great, they had to stop work. Later, the method of malaria transmission was invented, and the United States implemented various methods of preventing malaria and continued to dig the Panama Canal. As a result, the great project was a success.

Typhoid - In European and American countries 30 years ago, every year 30 several people out of 100,000 died by this illness. But after the finding this illness's spreading material is water and flies, they improve environment sanitation by force. The most important things are to settle faeces, improve water supply, and wipe off flies. In today, only 3 Americans die by this illness in every 100,000, just one British. But this illness still prevails in China, and nearly at least 30 people die by this illness. Can this show public health can reduce illness is a good example?

Plague - Plague will prevail in Fujian, Guangdong, and countries in Europe. In 14 century, one-quarter of people in Europe (near 2.5 million) die with this illness. Today the plague near doesn't exist in all the countries of Europe after using many kinds of preventive method. But a large pandemic happened in Fujian and Xinjiang in our country this year, and this can verify the value of preventive medicine.

The four examples above clearly tell us: To eliminate diseases and seek happiness for society and mankind, we should try our best to engage in various public health facilities. Now our government has the determination to promote health undertakings and is gradually developing them. However, we still hope that the whole country will work together to study and promote them, so that they can be widely promoted throughout the country. In this way, not only can diseases be eradicated, but also the status of the nation can rise steadily and be on par with the world's great powers. (End)

Local News

Central China, Communications, and Three Banks Issue Subsidiary Coins Today 111

Regulations for Acceptance and Exchange Without Restriction - The Mint Review Committee Will Hold a Regular Meeting on the 14th

According to the New Voice Press, after the Ministry of Finance announced the issuance of new subsidiary coins today, the Central Bank has already distributed the minted subsidiary coins to the Central Bank of China, the Communications Bank, and the two other banks, for simultaneous issuance and circulation in the market today, in accordance with the provisions of the regulations. Details are as follows:

Issued Today: The Central Mint has delivered five types of minted subsidiary coins, including copper half-cent and one-cent, and nickel five-cent, ten-cent, and twenty-cent coins, to the Central Bank for exclusive issuance. At the same time, the Central Bank will distribute them to the Central Bank of China, the Communications Bank, and the two other banks for simultaneous issuance today. All businesses can exchange new subsidiary coins for legal tender at face value at the Central Bank of China, the Communications Bank, and the two other banks. The Ministry of Finance will also distribute samples of the new subsidiary coins to the silver and money trade associations for reference.

Regulations for Acceptance: Article 5 of the Subsidiary Coin Regulations stipulates: "The number of subsidiary coins to be accepted in each transaction is limited to 20 yuan in legal tender for nickel coins (five-cent, ten-cent, and twenty-cent), and 5 yuan in legal tender for copper coins (half-cent and one-cent). However, this restriction does not apply to the collection of taxes and the exchange at the Central Bank." Article 7 stipulates: "If subsidiary coins are naturally worn out due to prolonged use, resulting in a reduction of 5% of the legal weight, they may be exchanged for new coins at the Central Bank."

Old Coins Still in Use: The existing circulating subsidiary coins will be recovered by the Ministry of Finance for destruction and reminting, but within a prescribed period, they will still be allowed to circulate at market prices. The measures and time limit will be determined by the Ministry of Finance by order. The number of new subsidiary coins per yuan of legal tender is as follows: five twenty-cent nickel coins, ten ten-cent nickel coins, twenty five-cent nickel coins, one hundred one-cent copper coins, and two hundred half-cent copper coins.

Regular Meeting of the Review Committee: The Central Mint Review Committee has scheduled a regular meeting for 4:30 PM on February 14th, to be held on the third floor of the Central Bank, to report on the review process for the previous month. In addition, the Central Mint is operating day and night, except for Sundays, to rush-mint new subsidiary coins to meet market demand.

Telegram Bureau to Implement Telephone Telegraph Service Starting on the 16th 119

Trial Report Satisfactory After Three Months

According to the New Voice Press, the Shanghai Telegram Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, in order to facilitate users, specially launched a telephone telegraph service on a trial basis from November 16th of last year. For all business hours after 6:00 PM every day until 7:00 AM the next morning, and after 12:00 PM on Saturday, telegraphs can be sent. The telephone telegraph service is open all day on holidays. When sending a telegram, users can dial the telephone number 13082. After receiving a reply from the telegraph bureau, they must report their telephone number and account name clearly, hang up the phone, and wait for the telegraph bureau staff to notify them to send the telegram. After the user has finished transmitting the telegram, the telegraph bureau staff will repeat it once for confirmation. If the proofreading is correct, the recorded telegram will be handed over to the machine for transmission, and a copy will be prepared, indicating the amount of telegraphic charges to be collected, and a receipt will be issued, which will be delivered by the telegraph messenger to the original sender's address the next morning for personal review, signature, and stamping, and the telegraphic charges will be collected. Telegraphic account users of the telegraph bureau who use their residential telephone to send telegrams after business hours and include the telegraphic charges in the bill for monthly settlement must apply to the telegraph bureau in advance and start transmitting telegrams only after approval. Since the start of the trial reporting, users have felt very convenient, and for more than two months, telegram senders have been extremely enthusiastic. The bureau originally set the trial reporting period for three months. If the trial results are excellent, it will officially start reporting. According to reporters from the bureau yesterday, since the trial report started on November 16th, it has been three months as of the 16th of this month, and the trial results are very satisfactory. Therefore, the bureau will officially implement the telephone telegraph service starting on the 16th of this month.

Qingdao Industrial Observation Group Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Starting Today to Visit Factories 124

Intended to Visit Five Areas Divide into Groups to Conduct - According to Talks, Impressions Obtained in Beijing and Wuxi Were Excellent

The Qingdao Municipal Social Bureau and the industrial safety and hygiene observation group organized by the industrial sector went to Beijing at the beginning of this month to visit the Central Factory Inspection Office and the industrial safety and hygiene exhibition jointly organized by the Ministry of Industry, and went to Wuxi to visit various factories. After completing their work, the entire group arrived in Shanghai at 11:00 PM the night before last. A New New Press reporter specially interviewed group member Chen Keyao yesterday morning. According to reports, the group's impressions and feelings obtained in Beijing and Wuxi were very detailed. The details are as follows:

Purpose of the Qingdao Industrial Group Organization: According to Mr. Chen, in the infancy of industry in China, all factories are only slightly rudimentary. If one wants to find a factory with comprehensive safety and hygiene equipment, there are not many to see. However, this equipment is extremely important to the factory itself and the welfare of the workers. The Central Factory Inspection Office, in view of this, specially launched an industrial safety and hygiene exhibition in Beijing to promote the attention of factories across the country. In order to seek sound factory organization, the Qingdao Municipal Social Bureau and industrialists originally had an industrial safety and hygiene association. This decision was made to improve facilities and specially organized an observation group to visit Beijing, and went to the most industrially developed areas in the country, Shanghai and Wuxi, to investigate the actual facilities of the factories, so as to learn from them.

Visiting the Industrial Safety Exhibition: After the members of the group arrived in Beijing to visit the exhibition, they gained excellent impressions. Most people's ideal is that without huge amounts of money, it is difficult to expect comprehensive safety and hygiene equipment. What we saw in Beijing are all easy and inexpensive, and can make the factory safe and worry-free. Each factory can imitate and carry out. Not only can many unfortunate accidents be reduced, but also the welfare of workers is not shallow. However, the exhibition is only held in Beijing, which is quite insufficient. After the factory has the above-mentioned equipment, the workers must also understand and cooperate in order to achieve perfection. Although it is not impossible for workers from various places to go to Beijing to visit, the number is limited. Most of them have not seen this actual phenomenon, which is difficult to popularize. Therefore, when we were in Beijing, we suggested to Minister Wu of the Ministry of Industry to hold the exhibition in various important industrial areas in order to achieve universality and achieve practical results. Minister Wu has already nodded in agreement and is planning to proceed. Once it can be put into practice, the national industry will definitely benefit a lot.

Impressions Gained from Various Factories in Beijing and Wuxi: In addition to visiting the exhibition in Beijing, the group went to various factories to conduct on-site inspections. They felt that the factories had considerable safety and hygiene equipment. It is agreed that the Jiangnan Automobile Company has the most comprehensive equipment and personnel management, which is highly commendable. After completing the work in Beijing, the group took a car to Wuxi on the 5th. After inspecting various factories in Wuxi, they had excellent impressions of the Huatong Silk Factory, the Shenxin Third Yarn Factory, and the Tongyi Machine Factory. It is agreed that Shenxin's labor autonomy has been particularly effective.

Visiting Shanghai Factories Today: When reporters asked about the itinerary in Shanghai, the answer was that today (i.e., yesterday) happened to be a regular Sunday holiday, and the colleagues were temporarily resting due to the fatigue of traveling. It was decided that tomorrow (starting today, we will contact various places to visit. The purpose of the visit is divided into five items, namely: A. Safety matters, building style of the factory, Taipingmen fire equipment training, the structure of boilers, the installation and protection of the engine, the installation and management of electrical money switch, the installation of power transmission, the protection of working machinery gears, B. Hygiene matters, about the factory's lighting ventilation temperature and humidity adjustment, about the processing and storage of toxic materials, about the absorption and cleaning of dust and powder, about the canteen, drinks, dormitory, toilet, medicine, and first aid, about epidemic prevention, vaccination, physical examination, and other hygiene, C. Worker welfare matters, worker working hours, rest holidays, and worker education, the treatment of female workers before and after childbirth, the work of female workers, child workers, and apprentices, worker savings insurance and cooperative entertainment, worker bonus distribution and worker injury, illness, and death allowances, about female workers' breastfeeding rooms, nurseries, and other welfare, D. Personnel management matters, the recruitment or employment of workers and apprentices, the contract regulations of workers and apprentices, the examination and rewards and punishments of workers, the job changes and layoffs of workers, the records of workers and apprentices, the training management of workers and worker organizations, E. General matters, about the history of the factory, and the current operating conditions, various organizations, manufacturing and production and sales, taxation, insurance, others, after the group completes the observation in Shanghai, they will gather the materials obtained from the visit, hold a meeting to discuss, and then decide what to do.
